When set, Envoy is able to\\n130:   //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\\n131:   //   this example sequence of updates:\\n132:   //\\n133:   //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\\n134:   //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\\n135:   //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\\n136:   //\\n137:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\\n138:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\\n139:   //   clean slate.\\n140:   //\\n141:   // * ``--dry-run-canary``. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\\n178: // the resource granularity.\\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\\n181: // connected to it.\\n182: //\\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\\n186: // debugging purposes only.\\n187: //\\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\\n189: // can be either or both of:\\n190: //\\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\\n195: //\\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\\n199: //\\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \\\"start\\\" of every\\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\\\";\\n209: \\n210:   // The node making the request.\\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\\n212: \\n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This does not need to be set if\\n215:   // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\\n216:   // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\\n217:   string type_url = 2;\\n218: \\n219:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\\n220:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\\n221:   // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\\n222:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\\n223:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\\n224:   //\\n225:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\\n226:   // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\\n227:   // added or removed to the resource list.\\n228:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\\n229:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\\n230:   //\\n231:   // .. note::\\n232:   //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\\n233:   //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them.   //\\n240:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\\n241:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\\n242: \\n243:   // A list of Resource names to remove from [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n257:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n258:   // along with each resource name.\\n259:   //\\n260:   // .. repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\\n265: \\n266:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\\n267:   // client to }\\n384: \\n385: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n386: message Resource {\\n387:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.Resource\\\";\\n388: \\n389:   // Cache other names that this resource can go by.\\n412:   repeated string aliases = 4;\\n413: \\n414:   // The resource level version. It allows xDS to track the state of individual\\n415:   // resources.\\n416:   string version = 1;\\n417: \\n418:   // The resource being tracked.\\n419:   google.protobuf.Any resource = 2;\\n420: \\n421:   // Time-to-live value for the resource. For each resource, a timer is started. The timer is\\n422:   // reset each time the resource is received with a new TTL. If the resource is received with\\n423:   // no TTL set, the timer is removed for the resource. Upon expiration of the timer, the\\n424:   // configuration for the resource will be removed.\\n425:   //\\n426:   // The TTL can be refreshed or changed by sending a response that doesn't change the resource\\n427:   // version. In this case the ``resource`` field does not need to be populated, which allows for\\n428:   // light-weight \\\"heartbeat\\\" updates to keep a resource with a TTL alive.\\n429:   //\\n430:   // The TTL feature is meant to support configurations that should be removed in the event of\\n431:   // a management server failure. When set, Envoy is able to\\n130:   //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\\n131:   //   this example sequence of updates:\\n132:   //\\n133:   //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\\n134:   //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\\n135:   //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\\n136:   //\\n137:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\\n138:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\\n139:   //   clean slate.\\n140:   //\\n141:   // * ``--dry-run-canary``. Additional\\n152:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\\n153:   // previous version on the stream prior to this ``DiscoveryResponse``, that were\\n154:   // unprocessed at response send time. Clients are expected to\\n165:   // remember the most recent error for a given resource across responses;\\n166:   // the error condition is not considered to be cleared until a response is\\n167:   // received that contains the resource in the 'resources' field.\\n168:   repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 7;\\n169: }\\n170: \\n171: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\\n172: // endpoint for Delta xDS.\\n173: //\\n174: // With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\\n175: // snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\\n178: // the resource granularity.\\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\\n181: // connected to it.\\n182: //\\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\\n186: // debugging purposes only.\\n187: //\\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\\n189: // can be either or both of:\\n190: //\\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\\n195: //\\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\\n199: //\\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \\\"start\\\" of every\\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\\\";\\n209: \\n210:   // The node making the request.\\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\\n212: \\n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. Clients that populate this\n84:   // field must be able to handle responses from the server where resources\n85:   // are wrapped in a Resource message.\n86:   //\n87:   // .. note::\n88:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\n89:   //   in ``resource_names`` and others in ``resource_locators``.\n90:   //\n91:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators = 7;\n92: \n93:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\n94:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This is implicit\n95:   // in requests made via singleton xDS APIs such as CDS, LDS, etc. but is\n96:   // required for ADS.\n97:   string type_url = 4;\n98: \n99:   // nonce corresponding to ``DiscoveryResponse`` being ACK/NACKed. See above\n100:   // discussion on ``version_info`` and the ``DiscoveryResponse`` nonce comment. This\n101:   // may be empty only if:\n102:   //\n103:   // * This is a non-persistent-stream xDS such as HTTP, or\n104:   // * The client has not yet accepted an update in this xDS stream (unlike\n105:   //   delta, where it is populated only for new explicit ACKs).\n106:   //\n107:   string response_nonce = 5;\n108: \n109:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\n110:   // failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details`` provides the Envoy\n111:   // internal exception related to the failure. It is only intended for consumption during manual\n112:   // debugging, the string provided is not guaranteed to be stable across Envoy versions.\n113:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 6;\n114: }\n115: \n116: // [#next-free-field: 8]\n117: message DiscoveryResponse {\n118:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \"envoy.api.v2.DiscoveryResponse\";\n119: \n120:   // The version of the response data.\n121:   string version_info = 1;\n122: \n123:   // The response resources. These resources are typed and depend on the API being called.\n124:   repeated google.protobuf.Any resources = 2;\n125: \n126:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n127:   // Canary is used to support two Envoy command line flags:\n128:   //\n129:   // * ``--terminate-on-canary-transition-failure``. When set, Envoy is able to\n130:   //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\n131:   //   this example sequence of updates:\n132:   //\n133:   //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\n134:   //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\n135:   //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\n136:   //\n137:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\n138:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\n139:   //   clean slate.\n140:   //\n141:   // * ``--dry-run-canary``. When set, a canary response will never be applied, only\n142:   //   validated via a dry run.\n143:   //\n144:   bool canary = 3;\n145: \n146:   // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\n147:   // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the 'resources' repeated Any (if non-empty).\n148:   string type_url = 4;\n149: \n150:   // For gRPC based subscriptions, the nonce provides a way to explicitly ack a\n151:   // specific ``DiscoveryResponse`` in a following ``DiscoveryRequest``. Additional\n152:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\n153:   // previous version on the stream prior to this ``DiscoveryResponse``, that were\n154:   // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\n155:   // to ignore any further ``DiscoveryRequests`` for the previous version until a\n156:   // ``DiscoveryRequest`` bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\n157:   // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\n158:   string nonce = 5;\n159: \n160:   // The control plane instance that sent the response.\n161:   config.core.v3.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\n162: \n163:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n164:   // Errors associated with specific resources. Clients are expected to\n165:   // remember the most recent error for a given resource across responses;\n166:   // the error condition is not considered to be cleared until a response is\n167:   // received that contains the resource in the 'resources' field.\n168:   repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 7;\n169: }\n170: \n171: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\n172: // endpoint for Delta xDS.\n173: //\n174: // With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\n175: // snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\n178: // the resource granularity.\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\n181: // connected to it.\n182: //\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\n186: // debugging purposes only.\n187: //\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\n189: // can be either or both of:\n190: //\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\n195: //\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\n199: //\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \"start\" of every\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\";\n209: \n210:   // The node making the request.\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\n212: \n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This does not need to be set if\n215:   // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\n216:   // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\n217:   string type_url = 2;\n218: \n219:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\n220:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\n221:   // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\n222:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\n223:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\n224:   //\n225:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\n226:   // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\n227:   // added or removed to the resource list.\n228:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\n229:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\n230:   //\n231:   // .. note::\n232:   //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\n233:   //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\n234:   //   the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\n235:   //   to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\n236:   //\n237:   // These two fields can be set in any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``, including ACKs\n238:   // and ``initial_resource_versions``.\n239:   //\n240:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\n241:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\n242: \n243:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\n244:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\n245: \n246:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n247:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_subscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\n248:   // along with each resource name.\n249:   //\n250:   // .. note::\n251:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\n252:   //   in ``resource_names_subscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_subscribe``.\n253:   //\n254:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_subscribe = 8;\n255: \n256:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n257:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\n258:   // along with each resource name.\n259:   //\n260:   // .. note::\n261:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\n262:   //   in ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_unsubscribe``.\n263:   //\n264:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\n265: \n266:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\n267:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\n268:   // It will not be populated:\n269:   //\n270:   // * In the very first stream of a session, since the client will not yet have any resources.\n271:   // * In any message after the first in a stream (for a given ``type_url``), since the server will\n272:   //   already be correctly tracking the client's state.\n273:   //\n274:   // (In ADS, the first message ``of each type_url`` of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\n275:   // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\n276:   // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\n277:   map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\n278: \n279:   // When the ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` is a ACK or NACK message in response\n280:   // to a previous ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``, the ``response_nonce`` must be the\n281:   // nonce in the ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``.\n282:   // Otherwise (unlike in ``DiscoveryRequest``) ``response_nonce`` failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details``\n287:   // provides the Envoy internal exception related to the failure.\n288:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 7;\n289: }\n290: \n291: // [#next-free-field: 10]\n292: message DeltaDiscoveryResponse {\n293:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\n294:       \"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryResponse\";\n295: \n296:   // The version of the response data (used for debugging).\n297:   string system_version_info = 1;\n298: \n299:   // The response resources. ConstraintList and_constraints = 3;\n379: \n380:     // The inverse (NOT) of a set of constraints.\n381:     DynamicParameterConstraints not_constraints = 4;\n382:   }\n383: }\n384: \n385: // `type_url`: The resource type being requested\\n   - `resource_names`: List of specific resource names (empty means request all resources)\\n   - `node`: Node information identifying the Envoy instance\\n   - `version_info`: Version of last accepted configuration\\n\\n3. **Request Reception**: Control plane's `StreamAggregatedResources` handler receives the `DiscoveryRequest` and queries its configuration cache for matching resources\\n\\n4. **Response Generation**: Control plane sends `DiscoveryResponse` containing:\\n   - `resources`: List of google.protobuf.Any messages containing typed resource configurations\\n   - `type_url`: Matching the request type_url\\n   - `version_info`: New version of this resource set\\n   - `type_url`: The resource type being requested\\n   - `resource_names`: List of specific resource names (empty means request all resources)\\n   - `node`: Node information identifying the Envoy instance\\n   - `version_info`: Version of last accepted configuration\\n\\n3. **Request Reception**: Control plane's `StreamAggregatedResources` handler receives the `DiscoveryRequest` and queries its configuration cache for matching resources\\n\\n4. **Response Generation**: Control plane sends `DiscoveryResponse` containing:\\n   - `resources`: List of google.protobuf.Any messages containing typed resource configurations\\n   - `type_url`: Matching the request type_url\\n   - `version_info`: New version of this resource set\\n   - `nonce`: Unique identifier for this response\\n\\n5. **Response Processing**: Envoy's GrpcMux receives the response through `onDiscoveryResponse()`, decodes the resources using the registered OpaqueResourceDecoder, and calls the subscription callbacks with the decoded resources\\n\\n6. **ACK/NACK**: Envoy sends back a `DiscoveryRequest` with the same nonce and updated `version_info` to ACK the update, or includes `error_detail` to NACK\\n\\n7. **Delta Updates**: For incremental updates, the Delta RPC (`DeltaAggregatedResources`) uses `DeltaDiscoveryRequest` with `resource_names_subscribe`/`resource_names_unsubscribe` and `DeltaDiscoveryResponse` with only changed/removed resources\\n\\n### Key Type URLs\\n\\nCommon resource types that flow through this system:\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.listener.v3.Listener` (LDS)\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.cluster.v3.Cluster` (CDS)\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.route.v3.RouteConfiguration` (RDS)\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.endpoint.v3.ClusterLoadAssignment` (EDS)\\n\\nThe ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) allows multiplexing all these resource types on a single bidirectional stream, identified by the `type_url` field in each request/response.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

`start()`: Initiates stream with management server\\n  - `addWatch()`: Starts a configuration subscription for specific resources\\n  - `onDiscoveryResponse()`: Handles received discovery responses\\n- The concrete implementations in `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h` and `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h` manage the actual bidirectional stream using the gRPC async client\\n\\n**Base Templates:**\\n- `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2:source/common/config/subscription_base.h` provides a template-based subscription callback implementation\\n\\n### Configuration Update Flow\\n\\n1. **Subscription Initiation**: Envoy's `GrpcSubscriptionImpl::start()` calls `grpc_mux_->addWatch()` registering interest in resources of a specific type_url (e.g., type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.cluster.v3.Cluster)\\n\\n2. **Request Transmission**: The gRPC mux establishes a bidirectional stream to the control plane using the `StreamAggregatedResources` RPC and sends the initial `DiscoveryRequest` containing:\\n   - `type_url`: The resource type being requested\\n   - `resource_names`: List of specific resource names (empty means request all resources)\\n   - `node`: Node information identifying the Envoy instance\\n   - `version_info`: Version of last accepted configuration\\n\\n3. **Request Reception**: Control plane's `StreamAggregatedResources` handler receives the `DiscoveryRequest` and queries its configuration cache for matching resources\\n\\n4. **Response Generation**: Control plane sends `DiscoveryResponse` containing:\\n   - `resources`: List of google.protobuf.Any messages containing typed resource configurations\\n   - `type_url`: Matching the request type_url\\n   - `version_info`: New version of this resource set\\n   - `nonce`: Unique identifier for this response\\n\\n5. **Response Processing**: Envoy's GrpcMux receives the response through `onDiscoveryResponse()`, decodes the resources using the registered OpaqueResourceDecoder, and calls the subscription callbacks with the decoded resources\\n\\n6. **ACK/NACK**: Envoy sends back a `DiscoveryRequest` with the same nonce and updated `version_info` to ACK the update, or includes `error_detail` to NACK\\n\\n7. **Delta Updates**: For incremental updates, the Delta RPC (`DeltaAggregatedResources`) uses `DeltaDiscoveryRequest` with `resource_names_subscribe`/`resource_names_unsubscribe` and `DeltaDiscoveryResponse` with only changed/removed resources\\n\\n### Key Type URLs\\n\\nCommon resource types that flow through this system:\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.listener.v3.Listener` (LDS)\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.cluster.v3.Cluster` (CDS)\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.route.v3.RouteConfiguration` (RDS)\\n- `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.endpoint.v3.ClusterLoadAssignment` (EDS)\\n\\nThe ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) allows multiplexing all these resource types on a single bidirectional stream, identified by the `type_url` field in each request/response.\"\n}\n","numLines":101,"startLine":1,"totalLines":101}}}
